    69	static struct winsize ws;
    70	size_t progress_printed; /* Printed chars in screen-wide progress bar. */
    71	size_t progress_full;    /* How many chars to write to fill the progress bar. */
    72	
    73	void memtest_progress_start(char *title, int pass) {
    74	    int j;
    75	
    76	    printf("\x1b[H\x1b[2J"); /* Cursor home, clear screen. */
    77	    /* Fill with dots. */
    78	    for (j = 0; j < ws.ws_col * (ws.ws_row - 2); j++) printf(".");
    79	    printf("Please keep the test running several minutes per GB of memory.\n");
    80	    printf("Also check http://www.memtest86.com/ and http://pyropus.ca/software/memtester/");
    81	    printf("\x1b[H\x1b[2K");          /* Cursor home, clear current line.  */
    82	    printf("%s [%d]\n", title, pass); /* Print title. */
    83	    progress_printed = 0;
    84	    progress_full = (size_t)ws.ws_col * (ws.ws_row - 3);
    85	    fflush(stdout);
    86	}
    87	
    88	void memtest_progress_end(void) {
    89	    printf("\x1b[H\x1b[2J"); /* Cursor home, clear screen. */
    90	}
    91	
    92	void memtest_progress_step(size_t curr, size_t size, char c) {
    93	    size_t chars = ((unsigned long long)curr * progress_full) / size, j;
    94	
    95	    for (j = 0; j < chars - progress_printed; j++) printf("%c", c);
    96	    progress_printed = chars;
    97	    fflush(stdout);
    98	}
    99	
   100	/* Test that addressing is fine. Every location is populated with its own
   101	 * address, and finally verified. This test is very fast but may detect
   102	 * ASAP big issues with the memory subsystem. */
   103	int memtest_addressing(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
   104	    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long);
   105	    unsigned long j, *p;
   106	
   107	    /* Fill */
   108	    p = l;
   109	    for (j = 0; j < words; j++) {
   110	        *p = (unsigned long)p;
   111	        p++;
   112	        if ((j & 0xffff) == 0 && interactive) memtest_progress_step(j, words * 2, 'A');
   113	    }
   114	    /* Test */
   115	    p = l;
   116	    for (j = 0; j < words; j++) {
   117	        if (*p != (unsigned long)p) {
   118	            if (interactive) {
   119	                printf("\n*** MEMORY ADDRESSING ERROR: %p contains %lu\n", (void *)p, *p);
   120	                exit(1);
   121	            }
   122	            return 1;
   123	        }
   124	        p++;
   125	        if ((j & 0xffff) == 0 && interactive) memtest_progress_step(j + words, words * 2, 'A');
   126	    }
   127	    return 0;
   128	}
   129	
   130	/* Fill words stepping a single page at every write, so we continue to
   131	 * touch all the pages in the smallest amount of time reducing the
   132	 * effectiveness of caches, and making it hard for the OS to transfer
   133	 * pages on the swap.
   134	 *
   135	 * In this test we can't call rand() since the system may be completely
   136	 * unable to handle library calls, so we have to resort to our own
   137	 * PRNG that only uses local state. We use an xorshift* PRNG. */
   138	#define xorshift64star_next()                         \
   139	    do {                                              \
   140	        rseed ^= rseed >> 12;                         \
   141	        rseed ^= rseed << 25;                         \
   142	        rseed ^= rseed >> 27;                         \
   143	        rout = rseed * UINT64_C(2685821657736338717); \
   144	    } while (0)
   145	
   146	void memtest_fill_random(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
   147	    unsigned long step = 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
   148	    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
   149	    unsigned long iwords = words / step; /* words per iteration */
   150	    unsigned long off, w, *l1, *l2;
   151	    uint64_t rseed = UINT64_C(0xd13133de9afdb566); /* Just a random seed. */
   152	    uint64_t rout = 0;
   153	
   154	    assert((bytes & 4095) == 0);
   155	    for (off = 0; off < step; off++) {
   156	        l1 = l + off;
   157	        l2 = l1 + words;
   158	        for (w = 0; w < iwords; w++) {
   159	            xorshift64star_next();
   160	            *l1 = *l2 = (unsigned long)rout;
   161	            l1 += step;
   162	            l2 += step;
   163	            if ((w & 0xffff) == 0 && interactive) memtest_progress_step(w + iwords * off, words, 'R');
   164	        }
   165	    }
   166	}
   167	
   168	/* Like memtest_fill_random() but uses the two specified values to fill
   169	 * memory, in an alternated way (v1|v2|v1|v2|...) */
   170	void memtest_fill_value(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, unsigned long v1, unsigned long v2, char sym, int interactive) {
   171	    unsigned long step = 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
   172	    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
   173	    unsigned long iwords = words / step; /* words per iteration */
   174	    unsigned long off, w, *l1, *l2, v;
   175	
   176	    assert((bytes & 4095) == 0);
   177	    for (off = 0; off < step; off++) {
   178	        l1 = l + off;
   179	        l2 = l1 + words;
   180	        v = (off & 1) ? v2 : v1;
   181	        for (w = 0; w < iwords; w++) {
   182	#ifdef MEMTEST_32BIT
   183	            *l1 = *l2 = ((unsigned long)v) | (((unsigned long)v) << 16);
   184	#else
   185	            *l1 = *l2 = ((unsigned long)v) | (((unsigned long)v) << 16) | (((unsigned long)v) << 32) |
   186	                        (((unsigned long)v) << 48);
   187	#endif
   188	            l1 += step;
   189	            l2 += step;
   190	            if ((w & 0xffff) == 0 && interactive) memtest_progress_step(w + iwords * off, words, sym);
   191	        }
   192	    }
   193	}
   194	
   195	int memtest_compare(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
   196	    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
   197	    unsigned long w, *l1, *l2;
   198	
   199	    assert((bytes & 4095) == 0);
   200	    l1 = l;
   201	    l2 = l1 + words;
   202	    for (w = 0; w < words; w++) {
   203	        if (*l1 != *l2) {
   204	            if (interactive) {
   205	                printf("\n*** MEMORY ERROR DETECTED: %p != %p (%lu vs %lu)\n", (void *)l1, (void *)l2, *l1, *l2);
   206	                exit(1);
   207	            }
   208	            return 1;
   209	        }
   210	        l1++;
   211	        l2++;
   212	        if ((w & 0xffff) == 0 && interactive) memtest_progress_step(w, words, '=');
   213	    }
   214	    return 0;
   215	}
   216	
   217	int memtest_compare_times(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int pass, int times, int interactive) {
   218	    int j;
   219	    int errors = 0;
   220	
   221	    for (j = 0; j < times; j++) {
   222	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Compare", pass);
   223	        errors += memtest_compare(m, bytes, interactive);
   224	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   225	    }
   226	    return errors;
   227	}
   228	
   229	/* Test the specified memory. The number of bytes must be multiple of 4096.
   230	 * If interactive is true the program exists with an error and prints
   231	 * ASCII arts to show progresses. Instead when interactive is 0, it can
   232	 * be used as an API call, and returns 1 if memory errors were found or
   233	 * 0 if there were no errors detected. */
   234	int memtest_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes, int interactive) {
   235	    int pass = 0;
   236	    int errors = 0;
   237	
   238	    while (pass != passes) {
   239	        pass++;
   240	
   241	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Addressing test", pass);
   242	        errors += memtest_addressing(m, bytes, interactive);
   243	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   244	
   245	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Random fill", pass);
   246	        memtest_fill_random(m, bytes, interactive);
   247	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   248	        errors += memtest_compare_times(m, bytes, pass, 4, interactive);
   249	
   250	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Solid fill", pass);
   251	        memtest_fill_value(m, bytes, 0, (unsigned long)-1, 'S', interactive);
   252	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   253	        errors += memtest_compare_times(m, bytes, pass, 4, interactive);
   254	
   255	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Checkerboard fill", pass);
   256	        memtest_fill_value(m, bytes, ULONG_ONEZERO, ULONG_ZEROONE, 'C', interactive);
   257	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   258	        errors += memtest_compare_times(m, bytes, pass, 4, interactive);
   259	    }
   260	    return errors;
   261	}
   262	
   263	/* A version of memtest_test() that tests memory in small pieces
   264	 * in order to restore the memory content at exit.
   265	 *
   266	 * One problem we have with this approach, is that the cache can avoid
   267	 * real memory accesses, and we can't test big chunks of memory at the
   268	 * same time, because we need to backup them on the stack (the allocator
   269	 * may not be usable or we may be already in an out of memory condition).
   270	 * So what we do is to try to trash the cache with useless memory accesses
   271	 * between the fill and compare cycles. */
   272	#define MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS (1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long)))
   273	/* Random accesses of MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE are performed at the start and
   274	 * end of the region between fill and compare cycles in order to trash
   275	 * the cache. */
   276	#define MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE (1024 * 8)
   277	
   278	NO_SANITIZE("undefined")
   279	int memtest_preserving_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes) {
   280	    unsigned long backup[MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS];
   281	    unsigned long *p = m;
   282	    unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
   283	    size_t left = bytes;
   284	    int errors = 0;
   285	
   286	    if (bytes & 4095) return 0;     /* Can't test across 4k page boundaries. */
   287	    if (bytes < 4096 * 2) return 0; /* Can't test a single page. */
   288	
   289	    while (left) {
   290	        /* If we have to test a single final page, go back a single page
   291	         * so that we can test two pages, since the code can't test a single
   292	         * page but at least two. */
   293	        if (left == 4096) {
   294	            left += 4096;
   295	            p -= 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
   296	        }
   297	
   298	        int pass = 0;
   299	        size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
   300	
   301	        /* Always test an even number of pages. */
   302	        if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;
   303	
   304	        memcpy(backup, p, len); /* Backup. */
   305	        while (pass != passes) {
   306	            pass++;
   307	            errors += memtest_addressing(p, len, 0);
   308	            memtest_fill_random(p, len, 0);
   309	            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
   310	                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   311	                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   312	            }
   313	            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
   314	            memtest_fill_value(p, len, 0, (unsigned long)-1, 'S', 0);
   315	            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
   316	                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   317	                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   318	            }
   319	            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
   320	            memtest_fill_value(p, len, ULONG_ONEZERO, ULONG_ZEROONE, 'C', 0);
   321	            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
   322	                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   323	                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   324	            }
   325	            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
   326	        }
   327	        memcpy(p, backup, len); /* Restore. */
   328	        left -= len;
   329	        p += len / sizeof(unsigned long);
   330	    }
   331	    return errors;
   332	}
   333	
   334	/* Perform an interactive test allocating the specified number of megabytes. */
   335	void memtest_alloc_and_test(size_t megabytes, int passes) {
   336	    size_t bytes = megabytes * 1024 * 1024;
   337	    unsigned long *m = malloc(bytes);
   338	
   339	    if (m == NULL) {
   340	        fprintf(stderr, "Unable to allocate %zu megabytes: %s", megabytes, strerror(errno));
   341	        exit(1);
   342	    }
   343	    memtest_test(m, bytes, passes, 1);
   344	    free(m);
   345	}
   346	
   347	void memtest(size_t megabytes, int passes) {
   348	#if !defined(__HAIKU__)
   349	    if (ioctl(1, TIOCGWINSZ, &ws) == -1) {
   350	        ws.ws_col = 80;
   351	        ws.ws_row = 20;
   352	    }
   353	#else
   354	    ws.ws_col = 80;
   355	    ws.ws_row = 20;
   356	#endif
   357	    memtest_alloc_and_test(megabytes, passes);
   358	    printf("\nYour memory passed this test.\n");
   359	    printf("Please if you are still in doubt use the following two tools:\n");
   360	    printf("1) memtest86: http://www.memtest86.com/\n");
   361	    printf("2) memtester: http://pyropus.ca/software/memtester/\n");
   362	    exit(0);
   363	}

    85	/* ================================= Debugging ============================== */
    86	
    87	/* Compute the sha1 of string at 's' with 'len' bytes long.
    88	 * The SHA1 is then xored against the string pointed by digest.
    89	 * Since xor is commutative, this operation is used in order to
    90	 * "add" digests relative to unordered elements.
    91	 *
    92	 * So digest(a,b,c,d) will be the same of digest(b,a,c,d) */
    93	void xorDigest(unsigned char *digest, const void *ptr, size_t len) {
    94	    SHA1_CTX ctx;
    95	    unsigned char hash[20];
    96	    int j;
    97	
    98	    SHA1Init(&ctx);
    99	    SHA1Update(&ctx, ptr, len);
   100	    SHA1Final(hash, &ctx);
   101	
   102	    for (j = 0; j < 20; j++) digest[j] ^= hash[j];
   103	}
   104	
   105	void xorStringObjectDigest(unsigned char *digest, robj *o) {
   106	    o = getDecodedObject(o);
   107	    xorDigest(digest, o->ptr, sdslen(o->ptr));
   108	    decrRefCount(o);
   109	}
   110	
   111	/* This function instead of just computing the SHA1 and xoring it
   112	 * against digest, also perform the digest of "digest" itself and
   113	 * replace the old value with the new one.
   114	 *
   115	 * So the final digest will be:
   116	 *
   117	 * digest = SHA1(digest xor SHA1(data))
   118	 *
   119	 * This function is used every time we want to preserve the order so
   120	 * that digest(a,b,c,d) will be different than digest(b,c,d,a)
   121	 *
   122	 * Also note that mixdigest("foo") followed by mixdigest("bar")
   123	 * will lead to a different digest compared to "fo", "obar".
   124	 */
   125	void mixDigest(unsigned char *digest, const void *ptr, size_t len) {
   126	    SHA1_CTX ctx;
   127	
   128	    xorDigest(digest, ptr, len);
   129	    SHA1Init(&ctx);
   130	    SHA1Update(&ctx, digest, 20);
   131	    SHA1Final(digest, &ctx);
   132	}
   133	
   134	void mixStringObjectDigest(unsigned char *digest, robj *o) {
   135	    o = getDecodedObject(o);
   136	    mixDigest(digest, o->ptr, sdslen(o->ptr));
   137	    decrRefCount(o);
   138	}
   139	
   140	/* This function computes the digest of a data structure stored in the
   141	 * object 'o'. It is the core of the DEBUG DIGEST command: when taking the
   142	 * digest of a whole dataset, we take the digest of the key and the value
   143	 * pair, and xor all those together.
   144	 *
   145	 * Note that this function does not reset the initial 'digest' passed, it
   146	 * will continue mixing this object digest to anything that was already
   147	 * present. */
   148	void xorObjectDigest(serverDb *db, robj *keyobj, unsigned char *digest, robj *o) {
   149	    uint32_t aux = htonl(o->type);
   150	    mixDigest(digest, &aux, sizeof(aux));
   151	    long long expiretime = objectGetExpire(o);
   152	    char buf[128];
   153	
   154	    /* Save the key and associated value */
   155	    if (o->type == OBJ_STRING) {
   156	        mixStringObjectDigest(digest, o);
   157	    } else if (o->type == OBJ_LIST) {
   158	        listTypeIterator *li = listTypeInitIterator(o, 0, LIST_TAIL);
   159	        listTypeEntry entry;
   160	        while (listTypeNext(li, &entry)) {
   161	            robj *eleobj = listTypeGet(&entry);
   162	            mixStringObjectDigest(digest, eleobj);
   163	            decrRefCount(eleobj);
   164	        }
   165	        listTypeReleaseIterator(li);
   166	    } else if (o->type == OBJ_SET) {
   167	        setTypeIterator *si = setTypeInitIterator(o);
   168	        sds sdsele;
   169	        while ((sdsele = setTypeNextObject(si)) != NULL) {
   170	            xorDigest(digest, sdsele, sdslen(sdsele));
   171	            sdsfree(sdsele);
   172	        }
   173	        setTypeReleaseIterator(si);
   174	    } else if (o->type == OBJ_ZSET) {
   175	        unsigned char eledigest[20];
   176	
   177	        if (o->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_LISTPACK) {
   178	            unsigned char *zl = o->ptr;
   179	            unsigned char *eptr, *sptr;
   180	            unsigned char *vstr;
   181	            unsigned int vlen;
   182	            long long vll;
   183	            double score;
   184	
   185	            eptr = lpSeek(zl, 0);
   186	            serverAssert(eptr != NULL);
   187	            sptr = lpNext(zl, eptr);
   188	            serverAssert(sptr != NULL);
   189	
   190	            while (eptr != NULL) {
   191	                vstr = lpGetValue(eptr, &vlen, &vll);
   192	                score = zzlGetScore(sptr);
   193	
   194	                memset(eledigest, 0, 20);
   195	                if (vstr != NULL) {
   196	                    mixDigest(eledigest, vstr, vlen);
   197	                } else {
   198	                    ll2string(buf, sizeof(buf), vll);
   199	                    mixDigest(eledigest, buf, strlen(buf));
   200	                }
   201	                const int len = fpconv_dtoa(score, buf);
   202	                buf[len] = '\0';
   203	                mixDigest(eledigest, buf, strlen(buf));
   204	                xorDigest(digest, eledigest, 20);
   205	                zzlNext(zl, &eptr, &sptr);
   206	            }
   207	        } else if (o->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_SKIPLIST) {
   208	            zset *zs = o->ptr;
   209	            hashtableIterator iter;
   210	            hashtableInitIterator(&iter, zs->ht, 0);
   211	
   212	            void *next;
   213	            while (hashtableNext(&iter, &next)) {
   214	                zskiplistNode *node = next;
   215	                const int len = fpconv_dtoa(node->score, buf);
   216	                buf[len] = '\0';
   217	                memset(eledigest, 0, 20);
   218	                mixDigest(eledigest, node->ele, sdslen(node->ele));
   219	                mixDigest(eledigest, buf, strlen(buf));
   220	                xorDigest(digest, eledigest, 20);
   221	            }
   222	            hashtableResetIterator(&iter);
   223	        } else {
   224	            serverPanic("Unknown sorted set encoding");
   225	        }
   226	    } else if (o->type == OBJ_HASH) {
   227	        hashTypeIterator hi;
   228	        hashTypeInitIterator(o, &hi);
   229	        while (hashTypeNext(&hi) != C_ERR) {
   230	            unsigned char eledigest[20];
   231	            sds sdsele;
   232	
   233	            memset(eledigest, 0, 20);
   234	            sdsele = hashTypeCurrentObjectNewSds(&hi, OBJ_HASH_FIELD);
   235	            mixDigest(eledigest, sdsele, sdslen(sdsele));
   236	            sdsfree(sdsele);
   237	            sdsele = hashTypeCurrentObjectNewSds(&hi, OBJ_HASH_VALUE);
   238	            mixDigest(eledigest, sdsele, sdslen(sdsele));
   239	            sdsfree(sdsele);
   240	            xorDigest(digest, eledigest, 20);
   241	        }
   242	        hashTypeResetIterator(&hi);
   243	    } else if (o->type == OBJ_STREAM) {
   244	        streamIterator si;
   245	        streamIteratorStart(&si, o->ptr, NULL, NULL, 0);
   246	        streamID id;
   247	        int64_t numfields;
   248	
   249	        while (streamIteratorGetID(&si, &id, &numfields)) {
   250	            sds itemid = sdscatfmt(sdsempty(), "%U.%U", id.ms, id.seq);
   251	            mixDigest(digest, itemid, sdslen(itemid));
   252	            sdsfree(itemid);
   253	
   254	            while (numfields--) {
   255	                unsigned char *field, *value;
   256	                int64_t field_len, value_len;
   257	                streamIteratorGetField(&si, &field, &value, &field_len, &value_len);
   258	                mixDigest(digest, field, field_len);
   259	                mixDigest(digest, value, value_len);
   260	            }
   261	        }
   262	        streamIteratorStop(&si);
   263	    } else if (o->type == OBJ_MODULE) {
   264	        ValkeyModuleDigest md = {{0}, {0}, keyobj, db->id};
   265	        moduleValue *mv = o->ptr;
   266	        moduleType *mt = mv->type;
   267	        moduleInitDigestContext(&md);
   268	        if (mt->digest) {
   269	            mt->digest(&md, mv->value);
   270	            xorDigest(digest, md.x, sizeof(md.x));
   271	        }
   272	    } else {
   273	        serverPanic("Unknown object type");
   274	    }
   275	    /* If the key has an expire, add it to the mix */
   276	    if (expiretime != -1) xorDigest(digest, "!!expire!!", 10);
   277	}
   278	
   279	/* Compute the dataset digest. Since keys, sets elements, hashes elements
   280	 * are not ordered, we use a trick: every aggregate digest is the xor
   281	 * of the digests of their elements. This way the order will not change
   282	 * the result. For list instead we use a feedback entering the output digest
   283	 * as input in order to ensure that a different ordered list will result in
   284	 * a different digest. */
   285	void computeDatasetDigest(unsigned char *final) {
   286	    unsigned char digest[20];
   287	    uint32_t aux;
   288	
   289	    memset(final, 0, 20); /* Start with a clean result */
   290	
   291	    for (int j = 0; j < server.dbnum; j++) {
   292	        serverDb *db = server.db[j];
   293	        if (db == NULL || kvstoreSize(db->keys) == 0) continue;
   294	        kvstoreIterator *kvs_it = kvstoreIteratorInit(db->keys, HASHTABLE_ITER_SAFE | HASHTABLE_ITER_PREFETCH_VALUES);
   295	
   296	        /* hash the DB id, so the same dataset moved in a different DB will lead to a different digest */
   297	        aux = htonl(j);
   298	        mixDigest(final, &aux, sizeof(aux));
   299	
   300	        /* Iterate this DB writing every entry */
   301	        void *next;
   302	        while (kvstoreIteratorNext(kvs_it, &next)) {
   303	            robj *o = next;
   304	            sds key;
   305	            robj *keyobj;
   306	
   307	            memset(digest, 0, 20); /* This key-val digest */
   308	            key = objectGetKey(o);
   309	            keyobj = createStringObject(key, sdslen(key));
   310	
   311	            mixDigest(digest, key, sdslen(key));
   312	
   313	            xorObjectDigest(db, keyobj, digest, o);
   314	
   315	            /* We can finally xor the key-val digest to the final digest */
   316	            xorDigest(final, digest, 20);
   317	            decrRefCount(keyobj);
   318	        }
   319	        kvstoreIteratorRelease(kvs_it);
   320	    }
   321	}
   322	
   323	#ifdef USE_JEMALLOC
   324	void mallctl_int(client *c, robj **argv, int argc) {
   325	    int ret;
   326	    /* start with the biggest size (int64), and if that fails, try smaller sizes (int32, bool) */
   327	    int64_t old = 0, val;
   328	    if (argc > 1) {
   329	        long long ll;
   330	        if (getLongLongFromObjectOrReply(c, argv[1], &ll, NULL) != C_OK) return;
   331	        val = ll;
   332	    }
   333	    size_t sz = sizeof(old);
   334	    while (sz > 0) {
   335	        size_t zz = sz;
   336	        if ((ret = je_mallctl(argv[0]->ptr, &old, &zz, argc > 1 ? &val : NULL, argc > 1 ? sz : 0))) {
   337	            if (ret == EPERM && argc > 1) {
   338	                /* if this option is write only, try just writing to it. */
   339	                if (!(ret = je_mallctl(argv[0]->ptr, NULL, 0, &val, sz))) {
   340	                    addReply(c, shared.ok);
   341	                    return;
   342	                }
   343	            }
   344	            if (ret == EINVAL) {
   345	                /* size might be wrong, try a smaller one */
   346	                sz /= 2;
   347	#if BYTE_ORDER == BIG_ENDIAN
   348	                val <<= 8 * sz;
   349	#endif
   350	                continue;
   351	            }
   352	            addReplyErrorFormat(c, "%s", strerror(ret));
   353	            return;
   354	        } else {
   355	#if BYTE_ORDER == BIG_ENDIAN
   356	            old >>= 64 - 8 * sz;
   357	#endif
   358	            addReplyLongLong(c, old);
   359	            return;
   360	        }
   361	    }
   362	    addReplyErrorFormat(c, "%s", strerror(EINVAL));
   363	}
   364	
   365	void mallctl_string(client *c, robj **argv, int argc) {
   366	    int rret, wret;
   367	    char *old;
   368	    size_t sz = sizeof(old);
   369	    /* for strings, it seems we need to first get the old value, before overriding it. */
   370	    if ((rret = je_mallctl(argv[0]->ptr, &old, &sz, NULL, 0))) {
   371	        /* return error unless this option is write only. */
   372	        if (!(rret == EPERM && argc > 1)) {
   373	            addReplyErrorFormat(c, "%s", strerror(rret));
   374	            return;
   375	        }
   376	    }
   377	    if (argc > 1) {
   378	        char *val = argv[1]->ptr;
   379	        char **valref = &val;
   380	        if ((!strcmp(val, "VOID"))) valref = NULL, sz = 0;
   381	        wret = je_mallctl(argv[0]->ptr, NULL, 0, valref, sz);
   382	    }
   383	    if (!rret)
   384	        addReplyBulkCString(c, old);
   385	    else if (wret)
   386	        addReplyErrorFormat(c, "%s", strerror(wret));
   387	    else
   388	        addReply(c, shared.ok);
   389	}
   390	#endif
   391

  2025	static void killMainThread(void) {
  2026	    int err;

  2037	 * should be used only when it's critical to stop the threads for some reason.
  2038	 * Currently the server does this only on crash (for instance on SIGSEGV) in order
  2039	 * to perform a fast memory check without other threads messing with memory. */
  2040	void killThreads(void) {

Now I can see the issue. Let me look at the `memtest_preserving_test` function more closely, especially the backup array size and the memcpy call at line 304:

The stack trace shows the crash is at `memcpy` in `memtest_preserving_test` at line 304 of memtest.c (based on the original), which corresponds to:

```c
memcpy(backup, p, len); /* Backup. */
```

The issue is that `len` can be larger than `sizeof(backup)`. Let's check:

- `MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS (1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long)))` - on a 64-bit system, this is `1024 * (1024 / 8) = 1024 * 128 = 131072` words, which is `131072 * 8 = 1048576` bytes (1 MB).
- The ASAN error says "READ of size 1048576" which is exactly 1MB - the size of the backup buffer.

Now look at the logic in `memtest_preserving_test`:

```c
size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
```

Wait, `sizeof(backup)` returns the size in bytes. But `left` is also in bytes. So if `left > sizeof(backup)`, `len = sizeof(backup)`. That seems fine.

But wait - the issue is that `backup` is a VLA (variable-length array) allocated on the stack. Let me check:

```c
unsigned long backup[MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS];
```

`MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS` is `(1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long)))`. On 64-bit, `sizeof(long)` is 8, so this is `1024 * 128 = 131072` elements, each 8 bytes = 1,048,576 bytes. That's 1 MB on the stack!

The ASAN crash reads exactly 1,048,576 bytes, which is the full size of the backup buffer. The issue might be that `len` is set to `sizeof(backup)` but the actual memory region being tested could be smaller than that, and the memcpy reads beyond the valid memory region.

Wait, let me re-read the logic:

```c
size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
```

If `left > sizeof(backup)`, then `len = sizeof(backup)`. Then:

```c
if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;
```

So if `len` is exactly `sizeof(backup)` and `sizeof(backup) / 4096` is even, len stays the same. Then it does `memcpy(backup, p, len)` where `len = sizeof(backup)`.

But the real problem is: what if `left` (the remaining bytes to test) is smaller than `sizeof(backup)`? Then `len = left`. Then `len` could be adjusted down by 4096 if odd number of pages. Then `memcpy(backup, p, len)` copies `len` bytes from `p` to `backup`. That's fine.

But what if `left` is larger than `sizeof(backup)` and `sizeof(backup) / 4096` is even? Then `len = sizeof(backup)`. The memcpy copies `len` bytes. This should be fine as long as `p` has at least `len` bytes available. Since `left > sizeof(backup)`, `p` should have at least `sizeof(backup)` bytes available.

```c
int memtest_preserving_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes) {
    unsigned long backup[MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS];
    unsigned long *p = m;
    unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
    size_t left = bytes;
    int errors = 0;

    if (bytes & 4095) return 0;     /* Can't test across 4k page boundaries. */
    if (bytes < 4096 * 2) return 0; /* Can't test a single page. */

    while (left) {
        /* If we have to test a single final page, go back a single page
         * so that we can test two pages, since the code can't test a single
         * page but at least two. */
        if (left == 4096) {
            left += 4096;
            p -= 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
        }

        int pass = 0;
        size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;

        /* Always test an even number of pages. */
        if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;

        memcpy(backup, p, len); /* Backup. */
        ...
```

Now, `sizeof(backup)` = `MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS * sizeof(unsigned long)` = `(1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long))) * sizeof(long)` = `1024 * 1024` = 1048576 bytes.

So `len` can be at most 1048576. The `memcpy` reads `len` bytes from `p`. 

But here's a subtle issue: `end` is computed as:
```c
unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
```

If `bytes` is less than `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` (which is `1024 * 8 = 8192`), this would underflow! But there's a check `if (bytes < 4096 * 2) return 0;` so bytes >= 8192, but bytes could be exactly 8192, making `bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = 0`. That's fine.

```c

```

So `memtest_compare` takes a memory region and compares the first half with the second half. It's used to trash the cache. But when `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` is called, `end` is at `m + bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`. The compare reads `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` bytes starting from `end`. For this to be valid, we need `end + MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE <= m + bytes`, i.e., `m + bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE + MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE <= m + bytes`, which is `m + bytes <= m + bytes`. That's fine.

But wait, the `end` pointer is computed once at the beginning, but `m` (the original pointer) never changes. However, `p` changes as we iterate. The `end` is used for cache-trashing purposes - it's supposed to point to the end of the original memory region. But the issue is: during iteration, `p` moves forward, and eventually `p` could overlap with or go past `end`.

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the loop more carefully:

```c

    ...
    size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
    if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;

    memcpy(backup, p, len); /* Backup. */
    ...
    memcpy(p, backup, len); /* Restore. */
    left -= len;
    p += len / sizeof(unsigned long);

```

So `p` starts at `m` and moves forward by `len` each iteration. The issue is that `p + len` could go beyond `m + bytes` if `len` is not properly bounded.

Wait, `len = min(left, sizeof(backup))`. Then adjusted to be even pages. Then `left -= len` and `p += len/sizeof(long)`. Since `len` starts as `min(left, ...)`, and `left` is the remaining bytes, `len <= left`. After adjustment, `len` could be smaller (by at most 4096). So `len <= left` still holds, and `p + len <= m + bytes`. This should be fine.

But there's a subtlety: what if `sizeof(backup)` is not a multiple of 4096? Let me check: `MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS = 1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long))`. That's even, so `len` stays 1048576 when `left >= 1048576`.

Let me look at the `memtest_preserving_test` function signature and its usage in debug.c more carefully.

The function is declared as:
```c
int memtest_preserving_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes);
```

And called from debug.c:
```c
errors += memtest_preserving_test((void *)start_vect[j], size_vect[j], 1);
```

Note the cast: `(void *)start_vect[j]` - but `start_vect[j]` is `size_t`, not a pointer! This is casting an integer to a pointer. That's how the start address (from /proc/self/maps) is converted to a pointer.

Now let me think about the actual ASAN issue. The problem might be related to how ASAN handles the stack-allocated VLA `backup`. But that doesn't explain the "READ of size 1048576" error.

Actually, let me re-read the ASAN error:
```
READ of size 1048576 at 0x0000800f7000
```

The address `0x0000800f7000` - this looks like it could be a memory-mapped region. The memcpy is reading from this address. If this address is near the end of a mapped region, and the memcpy tries to read 1MB from it, it could read past the end of the mapped region into unmapped memory.

But wait, the code should only be testing regions listed in `/proc/self/maps`, with sizes computed from the maps file. The size should be accurate...

Unless there's a race condition: between reading `/proc/self/maps` and actually testing the memory, the memory could be unmapped (e.g., by another thread). But `killThreads()` is called before `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps()`, so other threads should be terminated.

Hmm, but `killThreads()` calls `pthread_cancel` and `pthread_join`. The threads might not be fully cleaned up immediately. However, the bio and IO threads are killed.

Let me look at another angle. The function `memtest_preserving_test` uses a huge stack buffer (1MB). Maybe the issue is that this large stack allocation combined with ASAN causes a stack overflow? But the error says "READ of size 1048576" not "stack overflow".

Actually, let me look at this more carefully. The `NO_SANITIZE("undefined")` attribute is applied to `memtest_preserving_test`. This suppresses undefined behavior sanitizer, but NOT address sanitizer. So ASAN is still active.

Now, I think the real bug might be simpler. Let me look at the `end` pointer:

```c
unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
```

If `bytes` is less than `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`, this computation wraps around (size_t is unsigned). But we have a check for `bytes < 4096 * 2` which returns 0. However, `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` is `1024 * 8 = 8192`, and `4096 * 2 = 8192`. So `bytes` can be exactly 8192. In that case `bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = 0`, and `end = m`. That's OK.

But what if `bytes` is, say, 12288 (3 pages)? Then `bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = 4096`, `end = m + 4096`. And `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` reads 8192 bytes from `end`, i.e., from `m + 4096` to `m + 12288`. That's within the region. OK.

Now, what about the `memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` calls? They read from `m` to `m + 8192`. This is always safe because `bytes >= 8192`.

So the cache-trashing reads should be fine.

Let me think about this differently. Maybe the issue is that `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps` is called from `doFastMemoryTest` which is called from `printCrashReport` which is called when there's already a crash. The server might be in a state where memory mappings are inconsistent.

But that doesn't make the ASAN error a false positive. The code should still not read invalid memory.

Let me look at the actual memcpy line more carefully. The line is:
```c
memcpy(backup, p, len); /* Backup. */
```

Where `backup` is a stack-allocated VLA of size ~1MB. The issue might actually be that `backup` is too large for the stack! In many systems, the default stack size is 8MB, and 1MB is a significant portion. But with ASAN, the stack might have extra red zones, making the effective stack usage much larger.

Wait, ASAN typically has a stack limit of about 256MB, so 1MB should be fine.

But actually, rethinking: the error says "READ of size 1048576" - this is about reading FROM the source (`p`), not writing to the destination (`backup`). The memcpy reads from `p` (some memory region) and writes to `backup` (on stack). The READ is the problem - it means `p` points to memory that isn't fully readable for 1048576 bytes.

So the question is: why would a region listed in `/proc/self/maps` with a certain size not be fully readable?

One possibility: the region might be larger than the actual usable memory. Looking at `/proc/self/maps`, the size is `end_addr - start_addr`. But there could be guard pages or partial mappings within that range.

Another possibility: the code might have a bug where `left` tracking gets confused. Let me trace through a specific scenario:

Say `bytes = 1048576 + 4096 = 1052672` (257 pages). The loop:

Iteration 1:
- `left = 1052672`
- `len = min(1052672, 1048576) = 1048576`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 256 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment
- `memcpy(backup, p, 1048576)` - reads from `m` to `m + 1048576`
- ... tests ...
- `memcpy(p, backup, 1048576)` - restores
- `left -= 1048576 = 4096`
- `p += 1048576 / 8 = 131072`

Iteration 2:
- `left = 4096`
- `left == 4096` triggers the special case: `left += 4096 = 8192`, `p -= 4096/8 = 512`
- So `p` goes back to `m + 1048576 - 512*8 = m + 1048576 - 4096 = m + 1044480`
- `len = min(8192, 1048576) = 8192`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 2 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment
- `memcpy(backup, p, 8192)` - reads from `m + 1044480` to `m + 1052672`. That's the last 8192 bytes of the region. Valid.
- ... tests ...
- `memcpy(p, backup, 8192)` - restores
- `left -= 8192 = 0`
- loop ends.

That seems fine.

Let me try another scenario: `bytes = 1048576` exactly (256 pages).

Iteration 1:
- `left = 1048576`
- `len = min(1048576, 1048576) = 1048576`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 256 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment
- `memcpy(backup, p, 1048576)` - reads entire region
- ... tests ...
- `memcpy(p, backup, 1048576)` - restores
- `left = 0`, loop ends.

Fine.

What about `bytes = 1048576 - 4096 = 1044480` (255 pages)?

Iteration 1:
- `left = 1044480`
- `len = min(1044480, 1048576) = 1044480`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 255 % 2 = 1`, so `len -= 4096 = 1040384`
- `memcpy(backup, p, 1040384)` - reads 254 pages
- ... tests ...
- `memcpy(p, backup, 1040384)` - restores
- `left -= 1040384 = 4096`
- `p += 1040384 / 8`

Iteration 2:
- `left = 4096`
- `left == 4096` triggers: `left = 8192`, `p -= 512`
- `len = 8192`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment
- `memcpy(backup, p, 8192)` - reads from `m + 1040384 - 4096 = m + 1036288` to `m + 1044480`. But wait, the last 8192 bytes should be `m + 1036288` to `m + 1044480`. That's within the region. OK.

Hmm, all these scenarios seem fine. Let me think about what could go wrong...

Actually, wait. Let me re-examine the `end` pointer computation for the cache-trashing:

```c
unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
```

During iteration 2 in the last scenario, `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` is called. `end = m + bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = m + 1044480 - 8192 = m + 1036288`. It reads 8192 bytes from `end`, i.e., from `m + 1036288` to `m + 1044480`. That's within the region.

And `memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` reads from `m` to `m + 8192`. Also fine.

   195	int memtest_compare(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
   196	    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
   197	    unsigned long w, *l1, *l2;
   198	
   199	    assert((bytes & 4095) == 0);
   200	    l1 = l;
   201	    l2 = l1 + words;
   202	    for (w = 0; w < words; w++) {
   203	        if (*l1 != *l2) {
   204	            if (interactive) {
   205	                printf("\n*** MEMORY ERROR DETECTED: %p != %p (%lu vs %lu)\n", (void *)l1, (void *)l2, *l1, *l2);
   206	                exit(1);
   207	            }
   208	            return 1;
   209	        }
   210	        l1++;
   211	        l2++;
   212	        if ((w & 0xffff) == 0 && interactive) memtest_progress_step(w, words, '=');
   213	    }
   214	    return 0;
   215	}
   216	
   217	int memtest_compare_times(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int pass, int times, int interactive) {
   218	    int j;
   219	    int errors = 0;
   220	
   221	    for (j = 0; j < times; j++) {
   222	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Compare", pass);
   223	        errors += memtest_compare(m, bytes, interactive);
   224	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   225	    }
   226	    return errors;
   227	}
   228	
   229	/* Test the specified memory. The number of bytes must be multiple of 4096.
   230	 * If interactive is true the program exists with an error and prints
   231	 * ASCII arts to show progresses. Instead when interactive is 0, it can
   232	 * be used as an API call, and returns 1 if memory errors were found or
   233	 * 0 if there were no errors detected. */
   234	int memtest_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes, int interactive) {
   235	    int pass = 0;
   236	    int errors = 0;
   237	
   238	    while (pass != passes) {
   239	        pass++;
   240	
   241	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Addressing test", pass);
   242	        errors += memtest_addressing(m, bytes, interactive);
   243	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   244	
   245	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Random fill", pass);
   246	        memtest_fill_random(m, bytes, interactive);
   247	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   248	        errors += memtest_compare_times(m, bytes, pass, 4, interactive);
   249	
   250	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Solid fill", pass);
   251	        memtest_fill_value(m, bytes, 0, (unsigned long)-1, 'S', interactive);
   252	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   253	        errors += memtest_compare_times(m, bytes, pass, 4, interactive);
   254	
   255	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_start("Checkerboard fill", pass);
   256	        memtest_fill_value(m, bytes, ULONG_ONEZERO, ULONG_ZEROONE, 'C', interactive);
   257	        if (interactive) memtest_progress_end();
   258	        errors += memtest_compare_times(m, bytes, pass, 4, interactive);
   259	    }
   260	    return errors;
   261	}
   262	
   263	/* A version of memtest_test() that tests memory in small pieces
   264	 * in order to restore the memory content at exit.
   265	 *
   266	 * One problem we have with this approach, is that the cache can avoid
   267	 * real memory accesses, and we can't test big chunks of memory at the
   268	 * same time, because we need to backup them on the stack (the allocator
   269	 * may not be usable or we may be already in an out of memory condition).
   270	 * So what we do is to try to trash the cache with useless memory accesses
   271	 * between the fill and compare cycles. */
   272	#define MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS (1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long)))
   273	/* Random accesses of MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE are performed at the start and
   274	 * end of the region between fill and compare cycles in order to trash
   275	 * the cache. */
   276	#define MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE (1024 * 8)
   277	
   278	NO_SANITIZE("undefined")
   279	int memtest_preserving_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes) {
   280	    unsigned long backup[MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS];
   281	    unsigned long *p = m;
   282	    unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
   283	    size_t left = bytes;
   284	    int errors = 0;
   285	
   286	    if (bytes & 4095) return 0;     /* Can't test across 4k page boundaries. */
   287	    if (bytes < 4096 * 2) return 0; /* Can't test a single page. */
   288	
   289	    while (left) {
   290	        /* If we have to test a single final page, go back a single page
   291	         * so that we can test two pages, since the code can't test a single
   292	         * page but at least two. */
   293	        if (left == 4096) {
   294	            left += 4096;
   295	            p -= 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
   296	        }
   297	
   298	        int pass = 0;
   299	        size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
   300	
   301	        /* Always test an even number of pages. */
   302	        if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;
   303	
   304	        memcpy(backup, p, len); /* Backup. */
   305	        while (pass != passes) {
   306	            pass++;
   307	            errors += memtest_addressing(p, len, 0);
   308	            memtest_fill_random(p, len, 0);
   309	            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
   310	                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   311	                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   312	            }
   313	            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
   314	            memtest_fill_value(p, len, 0, (unsigned long)-1, 'S', 0);
   315	            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
   316	                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   317	                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   318	            }
   319	            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
   320	            memtest_fill_value(p, len, ULONG_ONEZERO, ULONG_ZEROONE, 'C', 0);
   321	            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
   322	                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   323	                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
   324	            }
   325	            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
   326	        }
   327	        memcpy(p, backup, len); /* Restore. */
   328	        left -= len;
   329	        p += len / sizeof(unsigned long);
   330	    }
   331	    return errors;
   332	}

Now I see a potential issue! Look at line 299:

```c
size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
```

And line 302:
```c
if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;
```

If `len == 0` after this adjustment, the loop would be infinite because `left -= len` would leave `left` unchanged. But `len` should never be 0 because the minimum `len` before adjustment is 8192 (since `left == 4096` is handled specially, and `bytes >= 8192`).

But actually, I think the real issue is different. Let me look at the `end` pointer more carefully:

```c
unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
```

The problem is: `bytes` is `size_t` (unsigned). `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` is `1024 * 8 = 8192`. If `bytes < 8192`, this wraps around. But there's a check `if (bytes < 4096 * 2) return 0;` which ensures `bytes >= 8192`. So when `bytes == 8192`, `end = m`. That's fine.

But wait: what happens with the `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` call when `bytes == 8192`? `end = m`, and it reads `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` (8192) bytes from `m`. That's the entire region. `memtest_compare` compares the first half with the second half. This is fine.

OK, I need to think about this differently. Let me look at the actual ASAN crash address: `0x0000800f7000`. This is a relatively low address. Let me check if this could be near the end of a mapped region.

Actually, I think the issue might be this: when the server crashes, `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps` reads `/proc/self/maps` and gets the list of anonymous regions. But by the time it tests them, those regions might have been unmapped or resized. However, `killThreads()` is called first.

But actually, looking at the call chain:
1. `_serverAssert` (assertion failure)
2. `printCrashReport`
3. `doFastMemoryTest`
4. `killThreads()`
5. `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps()`

After `killThreads()`, other threads are cancelled. But the main thread continues. The memory mappings should still be valid for the main thread.

Let me look at this from a different angle. Maybe the issue is that the `backup` array on the stack is too large and ASAN's red zones around stack variables cause issues. But that would be a stack buffer overflow, not a "READ of size 1048576" from some heap/mmap address.

Actually, I just realized something. Let me re-read the PR description:

```
READ of size 1048576 at 0x0000800f7000
```

The size 1048576 is exactly `MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS * sizeof(long)` = 1MB. This is the size of the `backup` array. And the memcpy at line 304 is:

```c
memcpy(backup, p, len);
```

If `len` is 1048576, and `p` points to valid memory, this should work. The ASAN error says the read is at `0x0000800f7000`. That's `p`. The question is: why is `p` (or `p + 1048576`) not valid?

Let me check if maybe the issue is with `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)`. The `end` pointer could be invalid in some cases.

Actually, I just noticed something important. Look at `memtest_compare`:

```c
int memtest_compare(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
    ...
    l1 = l;
    l2 = l1 + words;
```

If `bytes` is `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` = 8192, then `words = 8192 / 8 / 2 = 512`. It compares `l[0..511]` with `l[512..1023]`. The total memory accessed is `bytes` = 8192 bytes starting from `l`. So `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` accesses `[end, end + 8192)`. 

Now, `end = m + bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`. So the access is `[m + bytes - 8192, m + bytes)`. This should be within the region `[m, m + bytes)`.

But wait! What if `p` has advanced beyond `end`? In the loop, `p` starts at `m` and moves forward by `len` each iteration. Eventually, `p` could be at an address that's past `end`. But `memtest_compare_times(end, ...)` still uses the original `end`, which should still be valid as long as the original memory region is intact.

Hmm, but the cache-trashing reads from `m` and `end` are done while `p` is being tested. The memory at `m` and `end` is also being modified during the test (since `memtest_fill_random(p, len, ...)` modifies memory at `p`, which could overlap with `m` or `end`).

Actually, the purpose of the cache-trashing is exactly to trash the cache by reading from `m` and `end` (the start and end of the region). This is fine as long as those addresses are still valid.

OK, let me take a step back and think about what could cause an ASAN "unknown-crash" on a read. ASAN detects:
1. Heap buffer overflow
2. Stack buffer overflow  
3. Global buffer overflow
4. Use after free
5. Use after return

An "unknown-crash" means ASAN detected something but couldn't classify it as one of the standard categories. This can happen with:
- Reading from memory that's not mapped at all
- Memory that was mmap'd and then munmap'd

So the issue is likely that `p` points to a memory region that was partially unmapped. But `killThreads()` should prevent other threads from unmapping memory...

Wait, I just realized something else. Let me look at the `/proc/self/maps` parsing. It filters for anonymous maps (`00:00` and `rw`). But there could be regions that are partially mapped - for example, a region that starts at a page boundary but where the last page is a guard page.

Actually, let me look at this from a completely different angle. Maybe the bug is simpler: maybe `len` can be 0, causing an infinite loop, and the ASAN error is just a secondary symptom.

If `left = 4096`, it becomes `8192`, `len = 8192`, fine.
If `left = 8192`, `len = 8192`, fine.
If `left = 12288`, `len = 12288`, `len / 4096 % 2 = 3 % 2 = 1`, `len = 8192`. Fine.
If `left = 16384`, `len = 16384`, `len / 4096 % 2 = 4 % 2 = 0`. Fine.

But what about `len = 0`? Could `len` ever be 0? Only if `left = 0` before the loop, but the loop checks `while (left)`. Or if `len = 4096` and then `len -= 4096 = 0`. But `len = 4096` would mean `left = 4096`, which is handled by the special case that changes it to `8192`.

Wait, what if `left = 4096` but `sizeof(backup) < 4096`? That can't happen because `sizeof(backup) = 1048576`.

I'm going in circles. Let me try to reproduce the issue.

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdint.h>
#include <limits.h>

#define MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS (1024 * (1024 / sizeof(long)))
#define MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE (1024 * 8)

#if (ULONG_MAX == 4294967295UL)
#define MEMTEST_32BIT
#elif (ULONG_MAX == 18446744073709551615ULL)
#define MEMTEST_64BIT
#else
#error "ULONG_MAX value not supported."
#endif

#ifdef MEMTEST_32BIT
#define ULONG_ONEZERO 0xaaaaaaaaUL
#define ULONG_ZEROONE 0x55555555UL
#else
#define ULONG_ONEZERO 0xaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaUL
#define ULONG_ZEROONE 0x5555555555555555UL
#endif

#define xorshift64star_next()                         \
    do {                                              \
        rseed ^= rseed >> 12;                         \
        rseed ^= rseed << 25;                         \
        rseed ^= rseed >> 27;                         \
        rout = rseed * UINT64_C(2685821657736338717); \
    } while (0)

void memtest_fill_random(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
    unsigned long step = 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
    unsigned long iwords = words / step;
    unsigned long off, w, *l1, *l2;
    uint64_t rseed = UINT64_C(0xd13133de9afdb566);
    uint64_t rout = 0;

    for (off = 0; off < step; off++) {
        l1 = l + off;
        l2 = l1 + words;
        for (w = 0; w < iwords; w++) {
            xorshift64star_next();
            *l1 = *l2 = (unsigned long)rout;
            l1 += step;
            l2 += step;
        }
    }
}

void memtest_fill_value(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, unsigned long v1, unsigned long v2, char sym, int interactive) {
    unsigned long step = 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
    unsigned long iwords = words / step;
    unsigned long off, w, *l1, *l2, v;

    for (off = 0; off < step; off++) {
        l1 = l + off;
        l2 = l1 + words;
        v = (off & 1) ? v2 : v1;
        for (w = 0; w < iwords; w++) {
#ifdef MEMTEST_32BIT
            *l1 = *l2 = ((unsigned long)v) | (((unsigned long)v) << 16);
#else
            *l1 = *l2 = ((unsigned long)v) | (((unsigned long)v) << 16) | (((unsigned long)v) << 32) |
                        (((unsigned long)v) << 48);
#endif
            l1 += step;
            l2 += step;
        }
    }
}

int memtest_compare(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;
    unsigned long w, *l1, *l2;

    l1 = l;
    l2 = l1 + words;
    for (w = 0; w < words; w++) {
        if (*l1 != *l2) {
            return 1;
        }
        l1++;
        l2++;
    }
    return 0;
}

int memtest_compare_times(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int pass, int times, int interactive) {
    int j;
    int errors = 0;

    for (j = 0; j < times; j++) {
        errors += memtest_compare(m, bytes, interactive);
    }
    return errors;
}

int memtest_addressing(unsigned long *l, size_t bytes, int interactive) {
    unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long);
    unsigned long j, *p;

    p = l;
    for (j = 0; j < words; j++) {
        *p = (unsigned long)p;
        p++;
    }
    p = l;
    for (j = 0; j < words; j++) {
        if (*p != (unsigned long)p) {
            return 1;
        }
        p++;
    }
    return 0;
}

int memtest_preserving_test(unsigned long *m, size_t bytes, int passes) {
    unsigned long backup[MEMTEST_BACKUP_WORDS];
    unsigned long *p = m;
    unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
    size_t left = bytes;
    int errors = 0;

    printf("bytes=%zu, sizeof(backup)=%zu, start=%p, end=%p\n", 
           bytes, sizeof(backup), (void*)m, (void*)end);

    if (bytes & 4095) return 0;
    if (bytes < 4096 * 2) return 0;

    while (left) {
        if (left == 4096) {
            left += 4096;
            p -= 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
        }

        int pass = 0;
        size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;

        if (len / 4096 % 2) len -= 4096;

        printf("left=%zu, len=%zu, p=%p, p+len=%p\n", left, len, (void*)p, (void*)((unsigned char*)p + len));

        memcpy(backup, p, len);
        while (pass != passes) {
            pass++;
            errors += memtest_addressing(p, len, 0);
            memtest_fill_random(p, len, 0);
            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
            }
            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
            memtest_fill_value(p, len, 0, (unsigned long)-1, 'S', 0);
            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
            }
            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
            memtest_fill_value(p, len, ULONG_ONEZERO, ULONG_ZEROONE, 'C', 0);
            if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
                memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
                memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
            }
            errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
        }
        memcpy(p, backup, len);
        left -= len;
        p += len / sizeof(unsigned long);
    }
    return errors;
}

int main() {
    // Test with various sizes
    size_t sizes[] = {8192, 12288, 16384, 20480, 40960, 1048576, 1048576+4096, 1048576+8192};
    for (int i = 0; i < sizeof(sizes)/sizeof(sizes[0]); i++) {
        size_t sz = sizes[i];
        printf("\n=== Testing %zu bytes ===\n", sz);
        unsigned long *m = malloc(sz);
        memset(m, 0, sz);
        int errors = memtest_preserving_test(m, sz, 1);
        printf("Errors: %d\n", errors);
        free(m);
    }
    return 0;
}

Let me look at a different approach. Maybe the problem is about the `NO_SANITIZE("undefined")` attribute. Actually, let me look at the actual error message again:

```
READ of size 1048576 at 0x0000800f7000
```

The size 1048576 matches `sizeof(backup)`. This suggests that `len` = `sizeof(backup)` = 1048576. The source address `p` = `0x0000800f7000`. The memcpy tries to read 1MB from this address.

If the memory region that `p` points to is smaller than 1048576 bytes, but `len` is set to 1048576, that would cause the ASAN error.

But how could `len` be 1048576 when the region is smaller? The code says:
```c
size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
```

If `left` (remaining bytes) is greater than `sizeof(backup)`, `len = sizeof(backup)`. Otherwise, `len = left`. So `len` should never exceed `left`, which is the remaining bytes to test.

Unless... `left` is somehow wrong. Let me check if there's an integer overflow or underflow in `left` computation.

At the end of the loop:
```c
left -= len;
p += len / sizeof(unsigned long);
```

If `len = 0`, then `left` doesn't change and `p` doesn't change, causing an infinite loop. But we established that `len` can't be 0.

What about the special case:
```c
if (left == 4096) {
    left += 4096;
    p -= 4096 / sizeof(unsigned long);
}
```

After this, `left = 8192`. Then `len = min(8192, sizeof(backup)) = 8192`. Then `len / 4096 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment. Then after the loop: `left -= 8192 = 0`. Loop ends. Fine.

But what if `left` is not exactly 4096 but something like 12288 (3 pages)?
- `len = min(12288, 1048576) = 12288`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 3 % 2 = 1`, so `len -= 4096 = 8192`
- After loop: `left -= 8192 = 4096`
- Next iteration: `left == 4096` triggers special case...

This works correctly as we saw in the test.

OK, I think I need to look at this from a completely different angle. Let me check if the issue might be in `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps` and how it handles the regions:

Now I notice something important: there's no bounds check on `regions`. If there are more than `MEMTEST_MAX_REGIONS` (128) anonymous maps, it will overflow the `start_vect` and `size_vect` arrays! But that doesn't explain the ASAN error.

Wait, actually, let me check the `end` pointer computation in `memtest_preserving_test` once more:

```c
unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
```

What if `bytes` is very large (close to `SIZE_MAX`)? Then `bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` would still be fine. But what if `bytes` is `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE - 4096`? Then `bytes < 4096 * 2` and the function returns 0. OK.

But wait: what if `bytes` is `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE + 4096`? Then `bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = 4096`, `end = m + 4096`. The cache-trashing reads 8192 bytes from `end`, i.e., from `m + 4096` to `m + 12288`. But the region is only `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE + 4096 = 12288` bytes. So `m + 4096 + 8192 = m + 12288`, which is exactly the end of the region. Fine.

The git history doesn't show any recent fix related to this issue. Let me check the redis repository for relevant commits. The PR description mentions this is from valkey-io/valkey. Let me look at what the actual fix should be.

Let me think about this more carefully. The ASAN error is:

```
READ of size 1048576 at 0x0000800f7000
```

This is a read of exactly 1MB (the backup buffer size) from some address. This happens in memcpy at line 304. The fact that it's exactly 1048576 suggests that `len = sizeof(backup) = 1048576`.

Now, when would `len` be set to `sizeof(backup)`? When `left > sizeof(backup)`. But if `left > sizeof(backup)`, that means there are more than 1048576 bytes remaining to test, which means the memory region is at least that large. So the read should be valid...

UNLESS the memory region is exactly 1048576 bytes, and `left = 1048576`, and `len = min(1048576, 1048576) = 1048576`. Then `len / 4096 % 2 = 256 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment. Then `memcpy(backup, p, 1048576)` reads 1048576 bytes from `p`. This should be valid since the region is 1048576 bytes.

But wait! What if `p` has advanced due to the special case? Let me trace through a scenario where the region is exactly `1048576 + 4096 = 1052672` bytes (257 pages).

Iteration 1:
- `left = 1052672`
- `len = min(1052672, 1048576) = 1048576`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 256 % 2 = 0`, no adjustment
- memcpy 1048576 bytes from `p = m`
- ... tests ...
- memcpy back
- `left = 1052672 - 1048576 = 4096`
- `p = m + 1048576`

Iteration 2:
- `left = 4096`
- Special case: `left = 8192`, `p = m + 1048576 - 4096 = m + 1044480`
- `len = min(8192, 1048576) = 8192`
- memcpy 8192 bytes from `p = m + 1044480`
- This reads from `m + 1044480` to `m + 1052672`. That's within `[m, m + 1052672)`. ✓

OK, this works fine.

Let me try another scenario. What if the region is `1048576 - 4096 = 1044480` bytes (255 pages)?

Iteration 1:
- `left = 1044480`
- `len = min(1044480, 1048576) = 1044480`
- `len / 4096 % 2 = 255 % 2 = 1`, so `len -= 4096 = 1040384`
- memcpy 1040384 bytes from `p = m`
- ... tests ...
- `left = 1044480 - 1040384 = 4096`
- `p = m + 1040384`

Iteration 2:
- `left = 4096`
- Special case: `left = 8192`, `p = m + 1040384 - 4096 = m + 1036288`
- `len = 8192`
- memcpy 8192 bytes from `p = m + 1036288`
- This reads from `m + 1036288` to `m + 1044480`. Within bounds. ✓

Still works.

- `end = m + bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = m + 1044480 - 8192 = m + 1036288`
- `memtest_compare_times(end, 8192, ...)` reads from `m + 1036288` to `m + 1044480`. ✓

- `len / 4096 % 2 = 3 % 2 = 1`, `len = 8192`
- memcpy 8192 bytes from `p = m`

- `p = m + 8192`

- `left = 4096` → `left = 8192`, `p = m + 8192 - 4096 = m + 4096`
- `len = 8192`

Alright, I've been very thorough and I can't find a logical bug in the loop. Let me consider that maybe the issue is NOT in the loop logic but rather in something else.

Let me re-examine the ASAN error:

```
READ of size 1048576 at 0x0000800f7000
```

The memcpy at line 304 reads from `p`. The size 1048576 equals `sizeof(backup)`. This means `len = sizeof(backup)`. For `len` to be `sizeof(backup)`, we need `left > sizeof(backup)` (strictly greater) or `left == sizeof(backup)`.

If `left == sizeof(backup)`, then `len = sizeof(backup)` (since `left > sizeof(backup)` is false, `len = left = sizeof(backup)`).

So either `left >= sizeof(backup)`. In either case, there should be at least `sizeof(backup)` bytes remaining. So the read should be valid.

The only way this could be invalid is if the memory region isn't actually fully mapped, i.e., if there's a hole in the middle of the anonymous mapping. But that shouldn't happen with normal anonymous mappings.

Wait, I just had another thought. What if the issue is that `p` points to a memory region that was previously tested and modified, and the restoration (memcpy at line 327) didn't fully restore it? But that would affect data integrity, not memory accessibility.

OK, let me look at this from yet another angle. Maybe the problem is that `bytes` is not what we think. In `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps`, the size is computed as `end_addr - start_addr` from `/proc/self/maps`. But what if `/proc/self/maps` shows a region that includes guard pages or other unmapped pages?

Actually, I think I finally see it! Look at the `/proc/self/maps` format. The addresses are virtual addresses. A region in `/proc/self/maps` like:

```
7f0000000000-7f0000100000 rw-p 00000000 00:00 0 
```

This is a 1MB anonymous mapping. But what if the kernel maps a region that's larger than what was requested? For example, `malloc` might use `mmap` to allocate a large region, and the kernel rounds up to page boundaries. But the region in `/proc/self/maps` should reflect the actual mapped region.

Hmm, but there's another possibility: `memtest_preserving_test` could be called with a `bytes` value that's larger than the actual accessible memory. The code in `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps` computes `size = end_addr - start_addr`. This should be accurate.

`start_vect[j]` is of type `size_t`. It's cast to `void *`. This is correct: the address from `/proc/self/maps` is being used as a pointer.

Actually, hold on. I just realized: there's a potential issue with how `memtest_compare` works when called via `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)`.

`memtest_compare(end, 8192, ...)` does:
```c
unsigned long words = bytes / sizeof(unsigned long) / 2;  // = 8192 / 8 / 2 = 512
l1 = l;  // = end
l2 = l1 + words;  // = end + 512
```

Then it compares `l1[0..511]` with `l2[0..511]`, i.e., `end[0..511]` with `end[512..1023]`. The total memory accessed is `end[0..1023]`, which is 8192 bytes. This is within `[end, end + 8192) = [m + bytes - 8192, m + bytes)`. ✓

OK, I think I need to take a completely different approach. Let me look at the actual problem from the perspective of what a good fix would be.

Looking at the ASAN error once more:
```
READ of size 1048576 at 0x0000800f7000
```

The size is exactly 1MB, which is `sizeof(backup)`. The issue might be that the `backup` array is too large to be allocated on the stack, especially in the context of a crash handler where the stack might already be deep.

But the error is about reading from `p` (source), not writing to `backup` (destination). So the stack size isn't the direct issue.

Wait... unless the stack has grown so large that it overlaps with the memory region being tested! If the stack and the anonymous mapping are adjacent, and the stack grows into the mapping, then reading from `p` might actually be reading from stack memory that ASAN considers invalid.

But that's far-fetched. Let me think about this differently.

Actually, I just realized I should check if the issue might be related to `memtest_compare_times` being called with `end` when `bytes` is just slightly larger than `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`. Let me trace through a specific scenario:

Suppose `bytes = 12288` (3 pages):
- `end = m + 12288 - 8192 = m + 4096`
- `memtest_compare_times(end, 8192, ...)` reads `[m + 4096, m + 12288)`. That's 8192 bytes. ✓
- But `memtest_compare` divides the region into two halves: `[m + 4096, m + 8192)` and `[m + 8192, m + 12288)`. It compares them. ✓

Now, during the first iteration, `p = m`, `len = 8192` (adjusted from 12288 because 3 pages is odd). The test modifies `[m, m + 8192)`, which overlaps with the first half of what `memtest_compare_times(end, ...)` reads! 

Specifically:
- `end = m + 4096`
- `memtest_compare_times(end, 8192, ...)` reads `[m + 4096, m + 12288)`
- But `p = m`, `len = 8192`, so the test modifies `[m, m + 8192)`
- The overlap is `[m + 4096, m + 8192)`

So the cache-trashing read accesses memory that's currently being modified by the test. The test writes values, then the cache-trashing reads them, then the test restores the original values. This should be fine because the cache-trashing just needs to access memory to trash the cache; it doesn't matter what values are read.

But wait: what if the test hasn't restored the memory yet when the cache-trashing reads it? Looking at the code:

```c
while (pass != passes) {
    pass++;
    errors += memtest_addressing(p, len, 0);
    memtest_fill_random(p, len, 0);
    if (bytes >= MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE) {
        memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
        memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, pass, 1, 0);
    }
    errors += memtest_compare_times(p, len, pass, 4, 0);
    ...
}
```

The cache-trashing (`memtest_compare_times(m, ...)` and `memtest_compare_times(end, ...)`) happens AFTER `memtest_fill_random` modifies the memory and BEFORE `memtest_compare_times(p, len, ...)` checks it. Then later, `memcpy(p, backup, len)` restores the original content. So yes, the cache-trashing reads modified memory, which is intentional.

But actually, this could cause a problem: what if `end` overlaps with `p` and the memory at `end` has been modified by `memtest_fill_random(p, len, ...)` in a way that creates an invalid pointer? No, `memtest_fill_random` just writes random values to memory; it doesn't create pointers.

Wait, I just had an insight! Let me look at the `end` pointer again:

```c
unsigned long *end = (unsigned long *)(((unsigned char *)m) + (bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE));
```

This is computed ONCE at the start. But `bytes` might be exactly equal to `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`, in which case `end = m`. Then `memtest_compare_times(end, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` reads from `m`. But `memtest_compare_times(m, MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE, ...)` also reads from `m`. So both cache-trashing reads are from the same location. That's wasteful but not harmful.

But what if `bytes` is between `MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE` and `2 * MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`? Then `end` points somewhere in the first half. And the test modifies memory at `p = m` with `len` up to `sizeof(backup)`. If `len > bytes - MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`, then `p + len` could extend past `end + MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE`? No, `p + len <= m + bytes` and `end + MEMTEST_DECACHE_SIZE = m + bytes`. So they both end at the same place.

Actually, wait. I think I finally see a potential issue. Let me look at the case where `bytes` is small, like `12288` (3 pages).

- `end = m + 12288 - 8192 = m + 4096`
- First iteration: `left = 12288`, `len = 8192` (adjusted down), `p = m`
- The test modifies `[m, m + 8192)`. This overlaps with `[end, end + 8192) = [m + 4096, m + 12288)`.
- `memtest_compare_times(end, 8192, ...)` reads from `end = m + 4096`. The memory at `[m + 4096, m + 8192)` has been modified by the test.
- `memtest_compare` compares first half (`[m + 4096, m + 8192)`) with second half (`[m + 8192, m + 12288)`).
- Since the first half was modified (by `memtest_fill_random`) but the second half wasn't, the comparison will likely find them different and return an error!
- But wait, `memtest_compare_times` returns errors, and these errors are accumulated. So the cache-trashing could actually produce false positive errors!

But that's a functional issue, not an ASAN crash. And the errors from cache-trashing are ignored? No, they're not:

```c

```

  - `memtest_compare_times(end, 8192, ...)` reads `[m + 12288, m + 20480)`. This has been modified! ✓
  - After loop: `left = 20480 - 16384 = 4096`, `p = m + 16384`
- Iteration 2: `left = 4096` → `left = 8192`, `p = m + 16384 - 4096 = m + 12288`
  - Test modifies `[m + 12288, m + 20480)`
  - `memtest_compare_times(end, 8192, ...)` reads `[m + 12288, m + 20480)`. Same memory being tested! But that's fine, the test restores after.
  - After loop: `left = 0`, done.

So the cache-trashing reads always access memory that's being tested. This is intentional - it's supposed to trash the cache.

But wait, I just realized something important. Look at iteration 2: `p = m + 12288` and `len = 8192`. The test backs up `[m + 12288, m + 20480)` to the stack, then modifies it, then restores it. But the cache-trashing reads from `end = m + 12288` with size 8192 during the test. This reads the MODIFIED memory (which hasn't been restored yet). That's fine for cache trashing.

After the loop, `memcpy(p, backup, len)` restores the original content.

Everything seems correct. I'm truly struggling to find the bug.

Let me look at this from a completely different perspective. Maybe the issue is NOT in `memtest_preserving_test` itself but in `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps`. Maybe it's selecting a region that it shouldn't, or the region size is wrong.

Let me check the `/proc/self/maps` parsing more carefully:

```c
while (fgets(line, sizeof(line), fp) != NULL) {
    char *start, *end, *p = line;

    start = p;
    p = strchr(p, '-');
    if (!p) continue;
    *p++ = '\0';
    end = p;
    p = strchr(p, ' ');
    if (!p) continue;
    *p++ = '\0';
    if (strstr(p, "stack") || strstr(p, "vdso") || strstr(p, "vsyscall")) continue;
    if (!strstr(p, "00:00")) continue;
    if (!strstr(p, "rw")) continue;

    start_addr = strtoul(start, NULL, 16);
    end_addr = strtoul(end, NULL, 16);
    size = end_addr - start_addr;
    ...
    regions++;
}
```

There's no check for `regions` exceeding `MEMTEST_MAX_REGIONS`. If there are more than 128 anonymous maps, `start_vect` and `size_vect` would overflow. But that would corrupt the stack, not cause a clean ASAN read error.

Also, there's no check for `size` being 0. If `start_addr == end_addr`, size = 0, and `memtest_preserving_test` would return 0 immediately (due to `bytes < 4096 * 2`).

Wait, I just thought of something. What if a memory region is listed in `/proc/self/maps` but between the time we read the maps file and the time we test the memory, the region is unmapped? This could happen if there's a race condition with a signal handler or another thread. But `killThreads()` is called before `memtest_test_linux_anonymous_maps`, so other threads should be dead.

However, `killThreads()` uses `pthread_cancel` which is asynchronous. The threads might not have fully cleaned up. But `pthread_join` waits for them to finish. So they should be dead by the time we test memory.

But what about the main thread? `killMainThread` checks if `pthread_self() != server.main_thread_id`. In the crash handler, we're in the main thread, so `killMainThread` does nothing. Good.

Wait! I just realized something. Let me look at the condition at line 299 again:

```c
size_t len = (left > sizeof(backup)) ? sizeof(backup) : left;
```

If `left == sizeof(backup)`, then `len = left = sizeof(backup)`. That's fine.

But what if `left` is greater than `sizeof(backup)`? Then `len = sizeof(backup)`. After the test iteration:
```c
left -= len;
p += len / sizeof(unsigned long);
```

Now `left` is reduced by `sizeof(backup)`. But `p` has advanced by `sizeof(backup)` bytes. In the next iteration, `len` will be computed based on the new `left`. This continues until `left < sizeof(backup)`.

The issue might be: what if there's a memory region that's, say, 1052672 bytes (257 pages)? Then:
- Iteration 1: `len = 1048576`, tests first 1048576 bytes
- Iteration 2: `left = 4096`, special case, `len = 8192`, tests last 8192 bytes
